Search within the title, abstract, claims, or full patent document: You can restrict your search to a specific field using field names.

Use TI= to search in the title, AB= for the abstract, CL= for the claims, or TAC= for all three. For example, TI=(safety belt).

Search by Cooperative Patent Classifications (CPCs): These are commonly used to represent ideas in place of keywords, and can also be entered in a search term box. If you're searching forseat belts, you could also search for B60R22/00 to retrieve documents that mention safety belts or body harnesses. CPC=B60R22 will match documents with exactly this CPC, CPC=B60R22/low matches documents with this CPC or a child classification of this CPC.

Find patents

Keywords and boolean syntax (USPTO or EPO format): seat belt searches these two words, or their plurals and close synonyms. "seat belt" searches this exact phrase, in order. -seat -belt searches for documents not containing either word.

For searches using boolean logic, the default operator is AND with left associativity. Note: this means safety OR seat belt is searched as (safety OR seat) AND belt. Each word automatically includes plurals and close synonyms. Adjacent words that are implicitly ANDed together, such as (safety belt), are treated as a phrase when generating synonyms.

Compositions and methods for hydroxylating epothilones

Abstract
translated from

Isolated nucleic acid sequences and polypeptides encoded thereby for epothilone B hydroxylase and mutants and variants thereof and a ferredoxin located downstream from the epothilone B hydroxylase gene are provided. Also provided are vectors and cells containing these vectors. In addition, methods for producing recombinant microorganisms, methods for using these recombinant microorganism to produce hydroxyalkyl-bearing epothilones and an epothilone analog produced by a mutant of epothilone B hydroxylase are provided.

Figure 1 presents a diagrammatic illustration of epothilone B turning into Escherichia coli in actinomycete strain SC15847 (ATCC PT-1 0 4 3)-later identified as Amycolatopsis orientalis, described in WO 00/3 92 76 Biotransformation of Talimycin F. -8- (3) (3) 200418849 Cytochrome P-4 50 enzymes are present in prokaryotic and eukaryotic cells and collectively have a ^ heme binding function fn 'This functional site is associated with carbon monoxide After recombination, they can be distinguished by the absorption peak at 450 nm. Cytochrome P-4 50 enzymes can perform a wide range of oxidative reactions with alkanes on predominantly hydrophobic substrates, including aromatic and benzoic rings. In prokaryotes, they exist as a detoxification system and serve as the first enzymatic step to metabolize substrates such as toluene, benzene and camphor. Cytochrome P-450 enzymes are also present in secondary metabolite biosynthetic pathways, such as nikkomycin (Bruntner, C. et al., 1 999, Mol. Gen. Genet. 262) in Streptomyces tendae. 1 02- 1 1 4), doxorubicin (Dickens, ML, Strohl, WR, 1 996, J. Bacteriol, 1 7 8: 3 3 8 9-3 3 9 5) and epothilone Biosynthetic clusters (Julien, B. et al., 2000, Gene, 249: 153-16 0). With few exceptions, the cytochrome P-4 50 system is composed of three proteins in prokaryotes ... one is the iron redox protein NADH or NADH-dependent reductase, the other is iron-thioferredoxin and Cytochrome P-450 enzymes (Lewis, DF, Hlavica, P., 2000, Biochem. Biophys. Acta., 1 460: 3 5 3 -3 74). The electron system is transferred from ferredoxin reductase to ferredoxin and finally to the cytochrome P-450 enzyme to promote the division of molecular oxygen. To understand -13- (8) (8) 200418849, the term "alkyl" includes alkyl and substituted alkyls as defined herein. The term "alkyl" refers to a linear or branched, optionally substituted A chain-type saturated hydrocarbon group having 1 to 20 carbon atoms, preferably 1 to 7 carbon atoms. The expression "low-carbon alkyl group" refers to an optionally substituted alkyl group having 1 to 4 carbon atoms. The genomic fragment is then amplified by polymerase chain reaction (PCR). After PCR amplification, the reaction product was separated by gel electrophoresis and a fragment having a desired size was cut out. In a specific embodiment of the present invention, the polypeptide is intended to include the amino acid sequence of SEQ ID NO: 2 and a fragment or variant thereof that retains organisms that are substantially the same as this epothilone B hydroxylase Activity and / or function. In another embodiment of the present invention, the polypeptide is intended to include the amino acid sequence of SEQ ID NO: 4, and a fragment and / or variant thereof that retain substantially the same biological activity as this iron redox protein And / or features. A "variant", as used in the present invention, is intended to include its amino acid sequence with conservative amino acid substitutions relative to SEQ ID NO: 2 or 4, and it has been shown to exhibit similarity to SEQ ID NO: 2 Or 4 biologically active or functional polypeptide. "Conservative amino acid substitution" is intended to include aliphatic amino acids such as between Ala, Val, Leu and lie, between hydroxyl residues Ser and Thr, between acidic residues Asp and Glu, and amidine residues Asn Permutation with Gin. Exemplary amino acid sequences of the variants of the present invention are shown in SEQ ID NO: 4 3-4 9 and the amino acid substitutions of these exemplary variants are listed in Table 2 above. The term "mutant" as used herein is intended to include a nucleic acid sequence encoded by one or more point mutations, or deletions or additions of a nucleic acid, but still similar, as compared to SEQ ID NO: 1 or 3 A polypeptide having activity in the polypeptide encoded by SEQ ID NO: 1 or 3. In a preferred embodiment, a mutation in a nucleic acid is one that alters the specificity and / or yield of the polypeptide encoded by it. Proteins 23, 4 0 3-1 4, 1 99 5) and the like are generally described on the basis of the structure of the known homologous protein EryF (PDB Code 1 KIN chain A) to construct a three-dimensional model of epothilone B hydroxylase. The homogeneity between these sequences is 34%. FIG. 3 shows an alignment of an epothilone B hydroxylase sequence (SEQ ID NO: 2) and an EryF sequence (PDB Code 1KIN chain A; SEQ ID NO: 76). Figure 4 depicts a homogeneous model of epothilone B hydroxylase obtained from sequence alignment with EryF. -32- (27) (27) 200418849 In addition, an energy plot of epothilin B hydroxylase relative to EryF (PDB Code 1KIN) was also prepared and shown in FIG. 5. The average window size of 51 residues at a given residue position is used to calculate the average energy of the 51 residues in a sequence centered at the given residue. As shown in Figure 5, all the energies along the sequence are lower than 0, so it is obvious that the model construction shown in Figure 4 and Appendix 1 is reasonable. The three-dimensional structure shown in Fig. 4 epothilone B hydroxylase homogeneity model is defined by a set of structural coordinates listed in Appendix 1. The term "structural coordinates" refers to Cartesian coordinates derived from the construction of the homogeneous model. However, as known to those skilled in the art, a set of structural coordinates for a protein is a set of relative points of a shape defined within a three-dimensional shape. Therefore, a completely different set of coordinates may define a similar or identical shape. Furthermore, slight variations in individual coordinates, such as those using different alignment templates and / or different methods to generate similar homogeneous models in the generation of homogeneous models, will have a small impact on the overall shape. Variations in coordinates are also caused by mathematical calculations that construct the coordinates. For example, the structural coordinates listed in Appendix 1 may be calculated via fractionalization of the structural coordinates; addition or subtraction of integers from the structural coordinate group, inversion of the structural coordinates, or any combination thereof. Therefore, various computational analyses are required to determine whether a molecule or a part thereof is sufficiently similar to all or a part of the epothilone B hydroxylase described above to be regarded as the same degree. These analyses can be performed in existing software applications, such as SYBYL version 6.7 or INSIGHTII (Molecular Simulations Inc., San Diego, CA) version 2000 and user guides as attached (28) (28) 200418849 As described. For example, the overlap tool in the program SYBYL can be used to compare between different configurations and between different conformations of the same configuration. The procedure for comparing structures in S YB YL is divided into four steps: 1) loading the structures to be compared; 2) defining atomic equivalence in these structures; 3) performing a fitting operation; and 4) Analyze the results. Each construct is identified by a name. One structure was identified as the target (i.e., a fixed structure); the second structure (i.e., a mobile structure) was identified as the #source structure. Since the atomic equivalence in SYBYL is defined by user input, for the purposes of this aspect of the invention, equivalent atoms are defined as the protein backbone contained in all conservative residues between the two constructs to be compared Atoms (N, Ca, C, and 0). In addition, only rigid fit calculations are considered. When using the rigid fitting method, the operated structure is translated and rotated to obtain the best fit with the target structure. This fitting operation uses an algorithm that can calculate the best translation and rotation to be applied to the moving structure, so that the root mean square difference of the fitted for the specified equivalent atom pair is an absolute minimum . This case was reported by SYBYL in units of Angstrom (). For the purposes of the present invention, when any homogenous model of epothilone B hydroxylase overlaps with the corresponding backbone atom described in the structural coordinates listed in Appendix 1, its conservative residue backbone atom (N, C a, C , 0) Those with a root mean square difference less than about 4.0 A are considered to be the same. More preferably, the root mean square difference is less than about 3.0 A. More preferably, the root mean square difference is less than about 2.0 A. For the purposes of the present invention, any epothilone B hydroxylase homogeneous model-34- (29) (29) 200418849 overlaps with the corresponding backbone atom described in the structural coordinates listed in Appendix 1, its conservative residues The base skeleton atoms (N, C a, C, ) have root mean square differences less than about 2.0 A are considered to be the same. More preferably, the root mean square difference is less than about 1. A. In another specific example of the present invention, when the structural model in which the skeleton atom is replaced by other elements overlaps with the corresponding skeleton atom, those having a low root mean square difference are considered to be the same. For example, the homogeneous model of its original skeleton carbon and / or nitrogen and / or oxygen atoms replaced with other elements has approximately 4.0 A when overlapping with the corresponding skeleton atoms described in the structural coordinates listed in Appendix 1. The better is about 3.0 A, and even the better is about 2 A. The root mean square difference is considered to be the same. The term "root-mean-square difference" means the square root of the arithmetic mean of the square of the deviation from the mean . It is a way of expressing deviations or variations from a trend or a goal. For the purpose of the present invention, "root mean square difference" refers to the definition of the relevant part of a protein backbone relative to the backbone of the epothilone B hydroxylase moiety contained in the complex defined by the structural coordinates described herein. A variety of computational design methods based on structure have been disclosed in the art. For example, many computer modeling systems are available in which epothilone B hydroxylase sequences and epothilone B hydroxylase constructs (ie, epothilone B hydroxylase as provided in the Appendix) can be entered. The atomic coordinates of the enzyme and / or the atomic coordinates as provided above or within 10 A of the binding region). The computer system can then generate a structural detail of one or more of these areas that a potential epothilone B hydroxylase modulator can bind to so that the complementary structural details of the potential modulator can be determined accordingly. The design within these modeled systems is usually based on compounds capable of physically and structurally associating with epothilone B chemical enzymes. In addition to this -38-(33) (33) 200418849, the compound must be able to work out a conformation that allows it to associate with epothilone B hydroxylase. These modeled systems can estimate the potential inhibitory or binding effects of a potential epothilone B hydroxylase substrate or modulator before actual synthesis and testing. Methods for screening chemicals or fragments for their ability to associate with a given protein target are also well known. These methods often start without visually checking the joints on a computer screen. The selected fragment or chemical is then placed in the binding region of epothilone B hydroxylase. Docking is done using software such as INSIGHTII, QUANTA and SYBYL, followed by energy minimization and molecular dynamics using standard molecular mechanical force fields such as MMFF, CHARMM and AMBER. Examples of computer programs that are useful in the selection of chemical fragments or chemical bodies that can be used in the present invention include, but are not limited to, GRID (Goodford, 1 9 8 5), AUTODOCK (Goodsell, 1 990), and DOCK (Kuntz et al., 1 9 82) After selecting the better chemistries or fragments, they can be visually checked for their relationship with epothilone B hydroxylase and then assembled into a single potential modulator. Programs used to assemble individual chemicals include, but are not limited to, CAVEAT (Bartlett et al., 1 989) and 3D Database system (Martin 1 992) In addition, empty active sites can be used or a known inhibitor can be included as needed Some parts of the compound are de novo designed. Therefore, another aspect of the present invention relates to a recombinantly produced microorganism that can express epothilone B hydroxylase alone or together with ferredoxin and that the microorganism is capable of converting a compound having a terminal alkyl group, particularly It is epothilone, which is hydroxylated and made into a terminal hydroxyalkyl group. The recombinantly produced microbial silicon is produced by transforming a cell such as a bacterial cell using a plastid including a nucleic acid sequence encoding an epothilone B hydroxylase. In a preferred embodiment, the cell lines use a nucleic acid sequence comprising an epothilone B ase or a mutant or variant thereof, and a cell line located downstream of the epothilone B hydroxylase gene. The plastids of the nucleic acid sequence encoding the ferredoxin are transformed. Examples of microorganisms that can be transformed using these plastids to produce the recombinant microorganism of the present invention include, but are not limited to, E. coli, Bacillus megaterium, Streptomyces orientalis, -43- (38) (38) 200418849 Sorangiumce 11 u 1 osum, Rhodococcus erythropolis, and streptomyces species such as Streptomyces lividans, Streptomyces virginiae, Streptomyces venezuelae , Streptomyces a 1 bus, Streptomyces coelicolor, Streptomyces griseus and Streptomyces griseus o The recombinantly produced microorganisms of the present invention can be used in microbial programs or methods to produce Compounds with terminal hydroxyalkyl groups, and especially epothilones. Generally, a recombinantly-produced microorganism or a microorganism capable of selectively hydroxylating a terminal carbon or an alkyl group can be cultured in an aqueous nutrient medium containing assimilable carbon and nitrogen sources in the presence of an appropriate substrate under submerged aerobic conditions, or The enzymes derived from it produce hydroxyalkyl-loaded products. Suitable epothilones used as substrates in the method of the present invention may be any of these compounds having a terminal carbon or alkyl group capable of accepting the enzymatic hydroxylation of the present invention. The starting materials, or substrates, can be isolated from natural sources, such as P. cellulosae, or they can be synthetically formed epothilones. Any other substrate capable of accepting enzymatic hydroxylation with a terminal carbon or alkyl group can also be used in the method of the present invention. Microtubule stabilizers made using these compositions and methods can be used to treat a variety of cancers and other proliferative diseases including, but not limited to, the following: Cancer, including bladder, breast, colon, kidney, liver, lung , Ovary, pancreas, stomach, cervix, thyroid and skin; including squamous cell carcinoma; lymphoid hematopoietic tumors, including leukemia, acute lymphocytic leukemia, acute lymphoblastic leukemia, B-cell lymphoma , T-cell lymphoma, dgkins lymphoma, non-dgkins lymphoma, hair cell lymphoma, and Burketts lymphoma; tumors of mesenchymal origin, including fibrosarcoma and rhabdomyosarcoma, and other tumors, including melanoma, seminoma Semioma, Teratocarcinoma, neuroblastoma and glioma; tumors of the central and peripheral nervous system, including astrocytoma, neuroblastoma, glioma, and Schwannomas (schwa mas); mesenchymal tumors 'including fibrosarcoma, rhabdomyosarcoma and osteosarcoma; and other tumors' including melanoma , Xenderma pigmentosum, kefatoactanthoma, seminoma, thyroid follicular carcinoma and teratoma. The microtubule stabilizer prepared by using the composition and method of the present invention can also inhibit angiogenesis, thereby affecting tumor growth and providing treatment for tumors and tumor-related disorders. These anti-angiogenic -55- (50) 200418849 properties of these compounds can also be used to treat other conditions that are responsive to anti-angiogenic agents including, but not limited to, a blood blindness associated with retinal angiogenesis, Arthritis, especially inflammatory arthritis, multiple sclerosis, retinitis and psoriasis. The microtubule stabilizer prepared by using the composition and method of the present invention can induce or inhibit apoptosis, a physiological cell death process that is critical for normal development and homeostasis. Changes in the apoptotic pathway can contribute to the pathogenesis of many human diseases. The compounds of the present invention, such as those shown in I and 11 and Formula A, can be used to treat a variety of human diseases with apoptotic abnormalities when used as modulators of apoptosis, including, but not limited to, cancer and precancerous Lesions, immune response-related diseases, viral infections, degenerative diseases of the musculoskeletal system and kidney disease. Without wishing to be bound by any mechanism or morphology, microtubule stabilizers made using the compositions and methods of the invention can also be used to treat conditions other than cancer or other proliferative diseases. These conditions include, but are not limited to, viral infections such as herpes virus, scar virus, Epstein-Barr virus, Sindbis virus, and adenovirus; autoimmune diseases such as systemic lupus erythematosus, immune-mediated glomerulonephritis, rheumatic joints Inflammation, psoriasis, inflammatory bowel disease and autoimmune diabetes; neurodegenerative diseases such as Alzheimer's disease, AIDS-related dementia, Parkinson's disease, amyotrophic lateral sclerosis, pigmented retinitis, Spinal muscular atrophy and cerebellar degeneration; AIDS; Symptoms of Spinal Cord Dysplasia; Aplastic Anemia; Hemostatic Injury Associated with Myocardial Infarction; Stroke and Reinfusion Injury; Narrow SSS; Narrow Rhythm; Atherosclerosis Toxin-induced or alcohol-induced liver disease -56- (51) (51) 200418849 disease; hematological diseases such as chronic anemia and aplastic anemia; degenerative diseases of the musculoskeletal system such as osteoporosis and arthritis; aspirin- Sensitive sinusitis; cystic fibrosis; multiple sclerosis; kidney disease; and cancer pain. Example 14 4: Mass spectrometry The column eluate was directly introduced into the electrospray ion source of a ZMD mass spectrometer (Micromass, Manchester, UK). This instrument was calibrated using a Test Juice reference standard (Waters Corp., Milford, MA, USA) and delivered from a syringe pump (Harvard Apparatus, Holliston, M A, US A) at a flow rate of 10 l / min. The mass spectrometer operates with a low mass resolution of 13.2 and a high quality resolution of 11.2. Spectra were collected using a scan range of m / z 100 to 600 at an acquisition rate of 10 MS / sec. The ionization technology used is cationic electrospray (ES). The sprayer voltage was maintained at 2900 volts and the ion cone voltage was maintained at a potential of 17 volts. Example 17: Mutation Generation of the ebh Gene to Improve Yield or Change Specificity Using the Quikchange XL Site-Directed Mutagenesis Kit and Quikchange Multi Site-Directed Mutagenesis Kit from Stratagene to introduce mutations in the coding region of the ebh gene . Both methods use a 35-45 base DNA primer containing the desired mutation (SEQ ID NO: 5 4-5 9 fP 77), a methylated circular plastid template, and PfuTUr * b DNA polymerase (U.S. Patent Nos. 5,545,552 and 5,866,395 and 5,948,663) to produce a copy of a plastid template with mutations contained in mutation-generating primers. The reactant was subsequently digested with the endonuclease enzyme Dpnl to selectively digest the methylated plastid template, but left intact unmethylated mutant plastids. All procedures were followed by the manufacturer's instructions, except that the incubation time was increased from 1 hour to 3 hours during the Dpnl digestion step. The pPCRscript-ebh vector was used as a template for mutation generation. Transform 1 to 2 microliters of the reaction into XL 1-Blue electric competent cells or XL10-Gold super competent cells (SUatagene). The cells were plated on a 100 g / ml ampicillin plate of LA (Luria Agar) to a density of more than 100 colonies / plate, and incubated at 30 to 37 C for 24-48 hours. The entire plate was resuspended in 5 ml of LB containing 100 g / ml ampicillin. The plastids were directly separated from the resuspended cells by centrifuging the cells, and the plastids were then purified using a Mo Bio mini plastid preparation procedure -74- (69) 200418849
